    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText13764735110967705710" style="display:none">In plain black letters were the words Anthropological Research Facility,' but it was better known but another, less formal name. Most people just called it The Body Farm.The victim has been bound and torturer, the body decomposed beyond recognition...A second body is found.<br /><br />In America to escape the violence that nearly killed him, forensics expert David Hunter needs to know whether he is still up to the job of confronting death in all its strange and terrible forms.<br /><br />Then a body is found in a remote cabin out in the woods. And then another...<br /><br />Pushed deep into the heart of a terrifying manhunt, Hunter begins to wonder if they're on the trail of a maniac who simply cannot be stopped.<br /><br />Shocking, cunning and heart-stoppingly exciting, here is the new crime thriller from a No. 1 intentional bestselling storyteller.<br /><br />(back cover)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8957351649246890459">I think this is my favorite book of the series so far!<br/>The writing style was amazing and easy to read as always. The characters were realistic and well developed. The storyline was fantastic and exciting, without being too over the top.<br/>Something I love in every book I read by this author, is how well researched everything seems. I once again felt like I've learnt tons of new stuff. <br/>Overall, a very entertaining, interesting and suspenseful reading experience.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2833955466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10318332717616224710">4.5*<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26024.Simon_Beckett' title='Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Simon Beckett</a>'s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/54603-david-hunter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dr. David Hunter series</a> is one of my favourites, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead__David_Hunter___3_' title='Whispers of the Dead (David Hunter, #3) by Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Whispers of the Dead</a> was another quality instalment.<br/>After the traumatic events at the conclusion of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1328721.Written_in_Bone__David_Hunter___2_' title='Written in Bone (David Hunter, #2) by Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Written in Bone</a>, Dr. Hunter has temporarily left England, to carry out research at the <a href='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Tennessee_Anthropological_Research_Facility' rel='nofollow noopener'>University of Tennessee Anthropological Research Facility</a> in Knoxville, TN, colloquially known as "The Body Farm", whose director is his good friend and mentor, Tom Liebermann. It's not long before the research is interrupted by the discove</span>
  <span id="freeText10318332717616224710" style="display:none">4.5*<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26024.Simon_Beckett" title="Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon Beckett</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/54603-david-hunter" rel="nofollow noopener">Dr. David Hunter series</a> is one of my favourites, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead__David_Hunter___3_" title="Whispers of the Dead (David Hunter, #3) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Whispers of the Dead</a> was another quality instalment.<br />After the traumatic events at the conclusion of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1328721.Written_in_Bone__David_Hunter___2_" title="Written in Bone (David Hunter, #2) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Written in Bone</a>, Dr. Hunter has temporarily left England, to carry out research at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Tennessee_Anthropological_Research_Facility" rel="nofollow noopener">University of Tennessee Anthropological Research Facility</a> in Knoxville, TN, colloquially known as "The Body Farm", whose director is his good friend and mentor, Tom Liebermann. It's not long before the research is interrupted by the discovery of a decomposing body in a forest cabin not far from Knoxville. Hunter assists the aging Dr. Liebermann with the investigation of the crime scene, but as he's a foreign national, only under the sufference of the local medical examiner and TBI Agent-in-Charge.<br />I found the change in setting from the usual British Isles locations fascinating, not so much the Body Farm itself, which makes only a cameo appearance, but the lush and mysterious forest-covered foothills of the Great Smoky Mountains in eastern Tennessee.<br />As always, the central character Dr. David Hunter is sympathetically portrayed as an intuitive specialist in his field, who has suffered more than his share of personal trauma, both connected to and unrelated to his career as a forensic anthropologist. I also appreciated other finely-tuned characterisations in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead__David_Hunter___3_" title="Whispers of the Dead (David Hunter, #3) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Whispers of the Dead</a> of characters inspiring affection, such as Tom Liedermann and his wife Mary, and those who do anything but.<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead__David_Hunter___3_" title="Whispers of the Dead (David Hunter, #3) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Whispers of the Dead</a> is perhaps more confronting from a content perspective than other novels in the series - prospective readers should know that there are an awful lot of decomposing human remains in this book, with quite vivid descriptions of both appearance and associated smells. It's entirely necessary to the plot, but won't be for the squeamish.<br />In conclusion, this was a gripping and fast read. Highly recommended for Dr. Hunter afficionados like myself, and those new to the series (although I would suggest reading in series order).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10318332717616224710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8177319778697333587"><b> A forensic puzzle turns into a disturbing, terrifying, and deadly game!</b><br/><br/><i>As we crept past, waved on by a stone-faced police officer, I saw onlookers crowding a bridge that spanned the highway, leaning on the railing to gawk at the entertainment below. Then it was behind us, and the traffic resumed its usual flow as though nothing had happened.<br/>Tom seemed more his old self on the drive back from the cemetery.   <span id="freeText8177319778697333587" style="display:none"><b> A forensic puzzle turns into a disturbing, terrifying, and deadly game!</b><br /><br /><i>As we crept past, waved on by a stone-faced police officer, I saw onlookers crowding a bridge that spanned the highway, leaning on the railing to gawk at the entertainment below. Then it was behind us, and the traffic resumed its usual flow as though nothing had happened.<br />Tom seemed more his old self on the drive back from the cemetery. There was a sparkle in his eyes that I knew meant he was intrigued by this latest twist. First fingerprints from a murder scene that belonged to a dead man; now the wrong body had been found in his grave. A puzzle like that was milk and honey to him.</i><br /><br />He couldn't have known that this was going to become a deadly game where anyone could be the next victim..... <br /><br />********<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead__David_Hunter___3_" title="Whispers of the Dead (David Hunter, #3) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Whispers of the Dead</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26024.Simon_Beckett" title="Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon Beckett</a> is the third book in the <i>David Hunter</i> series and is as riveting as the first two! There is an enormous amount of emotion surrounding the characters that is precisely entangled within the storyline, creating a unique and masterful psychological crime thriller. If you enjoy forensic science like I do, this is a series not to be missed. <br />It opens with a homicide that produces several puzzling pieces of forensic evidence that leads the Tennessee Bureau of Investigation and forensic anthropologists, Tom and David, on a horrific and terrifying game of cat and mouse. There's a sense of impending danger and horror around every corner that makes the story thrilling, shocking, and difficult to put down. I don't think it will be long before I read book number four, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7927358.The_Calling_of_the_Grave__David_Hunter___4_" title="The Calling of the Grave (David Hunter, #4) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Calling of the Grave</a>. With a name like that, how can I resist?! <br /></span>

<div id="review_155519953" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155519953" />
    <a title="Nikki-ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3099305-nikki-ann"><img alt="Nikki-ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262463737p2/3099305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155519953?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki-ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki-ann" href="/user/show/3099305-nikki-ann">Nikki-ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553817515" href="/book/show/6936435-whispers-of-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155519953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8819048903633978949">Whispers of the Dead is the third book in the David Hunter series and gives us a bit more background and history to Dr David Hunter as he returns to the Body Farm in Tennessee where he’d trained early on in his career. The Body Farm actually exists. I’d heard of it previously when Stephen Fry had visited there in one of his programmes. The author, Simon Beckett, has also been there. It’s what gave him the idea for the series.<br/><br/>This story is pretty gruesome and I was quite glad that smell-o-vision </span>
  <span id="freeText8819048903633978949" style="display:none">Whispers of the Dead is the third book in the David Hunter series and gives us a bit more background and history to Dr David Hunter as he returns to the Body Farm in Tennessee where he’d trained early on in his career. The Body Farm actually exists. I’d heard of it previously when Stephen Fry had visited there in one of his programmes. The author, Simon Beckett, has also been there. It’s what gave him the idea for the series.<br /><br />This story is pretty gruesome and I was quite glad that smell-o-vision hasn’t made its way to books, the description alone was enough to make me feel slightly queasy! This book isn’t for anyone with a weak stomach as you can almost imagine being there as you read on.<br /><br />I’d worked out… no, guessed… who the murderer was early on, but I couldn’t be sure (I could find no particular reason as to why I’d guessed at that person, but I think I was going for one of the most unsuspecting people). Then I was pretty sure that it wasn’t who I thought it was… but then I know how Simon Beckett is. Just when you think something is all wrapped up he throws in a curve ball and everything changes.<br /><br />As with all crime thrillers, there’s the expected (and the unexpected) twists and turns. One particular twist made me audibly gasp in shock. Simon Beckett really is that good.<br /><br />This book truly is gripping. Take a look at the back cover of my copy and you’ll see the crease marks from where I’ve been gripping it tightly while reading it! I read most of the book in a day. Every time I thought I’d put it down at the end of a chapter, I fell the need to read on, to find out what happens.<br /><br />Whispers of the Dead is another great addition to the David Hunter series. If you’ve read and enjoyed the first two books, then you’ll definitely enjoy this one. If you haven’t read any of them then why not?! I have read the books in order (which I think is the best way), but I do think each book would also work as standalone novel. However, Simon Beckett’s David Hunter series really is a top notch crime and forensic thriller, and I’d highly recommend not just this book but the whole series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8819048903633978949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15036688943926427806"><b>Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>This is the third in the <i>David Hunter</i> series, and for me, it's the weakest of the three. That's not to say it's a bad book or that I didn't enjoy it; it isn't and I did!<br/><br/>It was as gory, gruesome and morbidly fascinating as I expected it to be, but I felt it was missing the shocking intensity of the first two books. I guessed the killer early on, which although wasn't confirmed until the reveal, took some of the suspense out of it; I remember actually gasping at the reveals in the</span>
  <span id="freeText15036688943926427806" style="display:none"><b>Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br />This is the third in the <i>David Hunter</i> series, and for me, it's the weakest of the three. That's not to say it's a bad book or that I didn't enjoy it; it isn't and I did!<br /><br />It was as gory, gruesome and morbidly fascinating as I expected it to be, but I felt it was missing the shocking intensity of the first two books. I guessed the killer early on, which although wasn't confirmed until the reveal, took some of the suspense out of it; I remember actually gasping at the reveals in the previous books. I also didn't find the setting and atmosphere as creepily chilling as before.<br /><br />That said, although I was a little disappointed by this story in comparison to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46465.The_Chemistry_of_Death__David_Hunter___1_" title="The Chemistry of Death (David Hunter, #1) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chemistry of Death</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1328721.Written_in_Bone__David_Hunter__2_" title="Written in Bone (David Hunter #2) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Written in Bone</a>, it was still good and I look forward to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7927358.The_Calling_of_the_Grave__David_Hunter___4_" title="The Calling of the Grave (David Hunter, #4) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Calling of the Grave</a></span>

    <a title="NAT.orious reads ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54624224-nat-orious-reads"><img alt="NAT.orious reads ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606165351p2/54624224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2123009387?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NAT.orious reads ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NAT.orious reads ☾" href="/user/show/54624224-nat-orious-reads">NAT.orious reads ☾</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11743114507513410112">I am a huge fan of mysteries/thrillers & always on the lookout for a good new series. With <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead' title='Whispers of the Dead by Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Whispers of the Dead</a> I just found one. I haven't read Beckett's other two books (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1328721.Written_in_Bone' title='Written in Bone by Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Written in Bone</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46465.The_Chemistry_of_Death' title='The Chemistry of Death by Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Chemistry of Death</a>), but I checked to make sure my public library had copies of both so I can go grab 'em the next time I'm there (they do).<br/><br/>I liked the main character, forensic anthropologist David Hunter, & all the rest of the characters, too.   <span id="freeText11743114507513410112" style="display:none">I am a huge fan of mysteries/thrillers &amp; always on the lookout for a good new series. With <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead" title="Whispers of the Dead by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Whispers of the Dead</a> I just found one. I haven't read Beckett's other two books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1328721.Written_in_Bone" title="Written in Bone by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Written in Bone</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46465.The_Chemistry_of_Death" title="The Chemistry of Death by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chemistry of Death</a>), but I checked to make sure my public library had copies of both so I can go grab 'em the next time I'm there (they do).<br /><br />I liked the main character, forensic anthropologist David Hunter, &amp; all the rest of the characters, too. Beckett's writing is clear &amp; clean &amp; his plotting is excellent. <br /><br />Plenty of forensic details, plenty of suspense, plenty of bodies. Great atmosphere &amp; an interesting villain in a story with a number of unusual &amp; cool twists made this a great read. Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_436113521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436113521" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436113521?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436113521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10319050427598124921">Beckett turns the tables on what his fans are used to reading, moving his band of ever-new characters from the rural spots within the United Kingdom to Tennessee, more specifically the Body Farm in and around Knoxville. This move, genius in my mind, is poignant, as it is the place where Beckett, a reporter by profession, learned about forensic anthropology and can be said to have helped push along his idea for this series and its main character. Moving things to the US does little to change the </span>
  <span id="freeText10319050427598124921" style="display:none">Beckett turns the tables on what his fans are used to reading, moving his band of ever-new characters from the rural spots within the United Kingdom to Tennessee, more specifically the Body Farm in and around Knoxville. This move, genius in my mind, is poignant, as it is the place where Beckett, a reporter by profession, learned about forensic anthropology and can be said to have helped push along his idea for this series and its main character. Moving things to the US does little to change the fast-paced nature of the book or its characters. While some say the WOW factor was less present, I still found it enjoyable as the reader was given brief portions of the story from the killer's perspective, without revealing who that might be. Filled with much more forensics and medical/anthropological jargon, Beckett amazes the reader and really leaves them on the edge of their seat. Thrilling until the end with its own WOW factor, the third instalment will only annoy those who are too boxed in to enjoy variety.<br /><br />I will admit, I was drawn to Beckett's work when he was called "the UK's Jefferson Bass", an extraordinary author in his own right. This book is not only set precisely where Bass writes his own books (Bass being the former head and creator of U Tennessee's Body Farm), but reflects some of the people/characters used in Bass books (though names are different). I was drawn in and could not put the book down. There were times I wondered if I was reading a Bass novel. I think this branch off to Tennessee was a great experiment for Beckett, though I would hope we do not see the forensic anthropologist flying all over the world. Doubtful, I am sure. While I cannot wait to see what awaits in the fourth novel, I am sure that anyone wanting a little thrill in their reading, and who does not mind a little gore, ought to invest in Beckett, and then branch off into the Bass series and see what I mean.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Beckett. While not your BEST in the series, surely one that keeps pace with the other two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10319050427598124921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2946936395" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2946936395" />
    <a title="Jaksen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7233842-jaksen"><img alt="Jaksen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455934399p2/7233842.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2946936395?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaksen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaksen" href="/user/show/7233842-jaksen">Jaksen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7233842-jaksen?shelf=mystery-series">mystery-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2946936395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer126881717918610970">Another in the series featuring former UK-based, GP-turned-forensic specialist, Dr. David Hunter. In this one David’s over here, in the good old USA (or ‘over there,’ for foreign readers), doing some brush-up forensic work with an old mentor, and former professor at the Tennessee Body Farm, or Forensic Anthropology Facility at the University of Tennessee. David’s coming off a serious accident back home in the UK…<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ … in which he was badly injured, broke up with his girlfriend and is</span></span>
  <span id="freeText126881717918610970" style="display:none">Another in the series featuring former UK-based, GP-turned-forensic specialist, Dr. David Hunter. In this one David’s over here, in the good old USA (or ‘over there,’ for foreign readers), doing some brush-up forensic work with an old mentor, and former professor at the Tennessee Body Farm, or Forensic Anthropology Facility at the University of Tennessee. David’s coming off a serious accident back home in the UK…<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ … in which he was badly injured, broke up with his girlfriend and is presently being stalked by a crazy person. This all happens in the prior book in the series. So, understandably, David’s a bit on edge.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But as it turns out, his friend (and mentor) pulls him into a case in which victims, of all ages and sexes, are being found in strange, and increasingly gory, situations and locations. The evidence in each seems to contradict itself – a man who obviously bled out in a remote cabin, but the blood all around him isn’t his. In a related case, a body removed from a cemetery for closer forensic inspection, turns out NOT to be who the man who was supposedly buried. This goes on for quite a while and I kept wondering just HOW is Mr. Beckett going to explain all this? <br /><br />The book is also a grim and gory read in places; the descriptions almost made me chuck the book – and entire series – and say forgetaboutthis. But the writing is good; the characters are great, so I read on. Glad I did. With David at first on the sidelines – he’s only a visiting specialist – and then gradually getting drawn in, the tension ramps up, with scenes a’plentiful of the dead: on the body farm in varying stages of decomposition; in a remote cabin, grave or other creepy place; on a slab being autopsied or re-autopsied. The dead are, simply said, just about everywhere. <br /><br />There’s also enough detail to make things shockingly – or rather mundanely – real. Which I like. Tell me what David had for lunch, okay; tell me how David reacts on seeing the next victim, okay again. This is one of the books where the main character seems so down to Earth and real, you can imagine him being your next-door neighbor, just with a kind of unusual job. You borrow his lawnmower; he uses your hedge clippers. You tell him about your day at the office; he mentions how his went down at the mortuary. :D<br /><br />I will continue with this remarkable series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="126881717918610970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_162213196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162213196" />
    <a title="J.F. Juzwik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5142688-j-f-juzwik"><img alt="J.F. Juzwik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440713253p2/5142688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162213196?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.F. Juzwik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.F. Juzwik" href="/user/show/5142688-j-f-juzwik">J.F. Juzwik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162213196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9335551407834439832">Whispers of the Dead is a dark thriller, featuring Dr. David Hunter, a British forensic anthropologist. He leaves his native London for Tennessee with the purpose of conducting research at the legendary Body Farm, as well as to visit his mentor and director of the facility, Tom Leiberman. When Tom is called to assist with a homicide investigation, he wants David on his team.<br/><br/>The bodies begin to pile up, and trust me--the crime scenes are pictures you don't want in your head for too long. Danger l</span>
  <span id="freeText9335551407834439832" style="display:none">Whispers of the Dead is a dark thriller, featuring Dr. David Hunter, a British forensic anthropologist. He leaves his native London for Tennessee with the purpose of conducting research at the legendary Body Farm, as well as to visit his mentor and director of the facility, Tom Leiberman. When Tom is called to assist with a homicide investigation, he wants David on his team.<br /><br />The bodies begin to pile up, and trust me--the crime scenes are pictures you don't want in your head for too long. Danger lurks for members of the team, and needless to say, time is of the essence to find the individual responsible.<br /><br />I know what you're thinking: Another serial killer story--yawn! But, guess what. You're as wrong as you can be. The deeper I got into this, and the more I got to know of the characters, the harder it was to put down.<br /><br />This is not anywhere near the 'typical' psychopath/sociopath tale. You'll know that as soon as you start getting the story from the killer's point of view, which Beckett shares with us. The killer's thoughts and overall philosophy are creepy as hell, and believe me, you'll be turning those pages very quickly.<br /><br />This is an edgy mystery, extremely graphic, and the end packs a helluva wallop. And that's not all - snooping around to get some author info, I discovered that Whispers is the third in a series featuring Dr. Hunter. Now, if you're like me, about the time you're halfway through the second book in most series 'featuring' a specific character, you're searching the fine print for the killer's phone number so you can arrange for him to quietly, and permanently, dispose of this so-called 'recurring star' long before Book 3 is even drafted. There is nothing more tedious than reliving so-and-so's 'lonely' past, 'dismal' present, and 'bleak' future over and over and..., well, you get my drift. But, not so here. This is a solid three-dimensional character. He's not some flat Jack's-a-dull-boy dud forced upon you on every other page.<br /><br />Dr. Hunter's story begins in The Chemistry of Death and continues in Written in Bones. Haven't read these yet, but you can bet I'm pulling a hard reverse here to begin at the beginning with this doc. This is good stuff, people, and I recommend it highly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9335551407834439832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3928369885044365303" style="display:none">A lot like the previous two, but this one takes place on a bigger island - well, not exactly an island, per se, but if things keep on the way they're going, the US may become a political island.<br /><br />Lots of killing in this one, as expected from the first two. The killer seemed like he was so far ahead of his pursuers that it hard to imagine they'd ever catch him. But with a bit of luck, and David Hunter's analytical mind, they finally catch up with him, but there are a few surprises even at that late stage of the game, as you might expect if you've read the first two. <br /><br />The series seems to concentrate as much on the people as the crimes. Makes it a little slower than some people like, but I enjoy it. But now I need a break from this series. Too many people dying.</span>

This one was even gorier than the first two, a huge body count by the time David is finished, but it's superbly written and has an almost breathtaking climax. <div id="review_584644168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/584644168" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4894054-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312308187p2/4894054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/584644168?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/4894054-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584644168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9656663154184628133">Where oh where to start with this train wreck? Probably the most irritating of all are sections written in second person. Yep. That's right <i>
  <b>Second-Fricking-Person</b>
</i> Can there be anything that screams "Look at me! I'm writing!" than second person? If there is, please let me know. <br/><br/>And then there's one tiny bit that's written in third person. Just one little bit. Nothing else. What happened? Did he mean to change it to second person and just forgot? <br/><br/>No need to mention the two dimensional characte</span>
  <span id="freeText9656663154184628133" style="display:none">Where oh where to start with this train wreck? Probably the most irritating of all are sections written in second person. Yep. That's right <i>
  <b>Second-Fricking-Person</b>
</i> Can there be anything that screams "Look at me! I'm writing!" than second person? If there is, please let me know. <br /><br />And then there's one tiny bit that's written in third person. Just one little bit. Nothing else. What happened? Did he mean to change it to second person and just forgot? <br /><br />No need to mention the two dimensional characters and paper-thin plot. Unfortunately, I think those are becoming Mr. Beckett's hallmark.<br /><br />But! There are a few points that are so amazingly bad they <b>must</b> be mentioned. <br /><br />1. Londoner David Hunter visits the States yet there is absolutely NO mention whatsoever about driving on the right rather than the left. As someone who has experienced moving between the two countries, this is one of the first things you notice. As a matter of fact, I found that I had to sit sideways in the passenger's seat while back in the States to keep from grabbing for a non-existent steering wheel. While driving down small side streets (streets with no center line) I would have a momentary start when I would realize I was on the wrong side of the road. Crossing a busy street is also a problem--which way do you look for oncoming traffic? By some miracle, David Hunter has none of these problems. It's all so natural to him that he (or rather Beckett) doesn't bother mentioning it. Yeah. Right.<br /><br />2. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When a pregnant, about-to-deliver woman is found, Dr. Hunter stays behind while the police rush her to meet the ambulance. The reason--he trained as a GP rather than an obstetrician. What? He's a qualified doctor yet he "don't know nothing about birthin' no babies"? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Yeah. Right.<br /><br />3. People eastern Tennessee do not use <i>y'all</i> as a second person plural form. Y'all is used farther south and west--Texas, Louisiana, Georgia, etc. Here the preferred form is <i>you-uns</i>, and it is not used to refer to a single person as <i>y'all</i> is. This, coupled with Point #1, makes me wonder if Mr. Beckett has ever been to Knoxville--much less the States. Of course, he could have only met people who use y'all...some little pocket of displaced Texans. Yeah. Right.<br /><br />4. Then there's the problem....<br /><br />Never mind #4. You get the picture. I've already spent more time on this review than the book deserves. I'm not going to waste any more of your time except to say "Don't waste your time on this hunk of junk." </span>
  <a data-text-id="9656663154184628133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_164924243" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164924243" />
    <a title="Jennifer (JC-S)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/283014-jennifer-jc-s"><img alt="Jennifer (JC-S)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528085840p2/283014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164924243?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer (JC-S)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer (JC-S)" href="/user/show/283014-jennifer-jc-s">Jennifer (JC-S)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283014-jennifer-jc-s?shelf=librarybooks">librarybooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164924243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2224511821542738235">‘Skin. The largest human organ, it is also the most overlooked.’<br/>Dr David Hunter is still recovering from a near-fatal attack, and has left London temporarily to spend time at the Anthropology Research Facility in Knoxville, Tennessee.<br/> <br/>‘Most people just called it the Body Farm’.<br/><br/>This is where David Hunter first trained in forensic anthropology, and he hopes that this return trip will restore his shattered confidence and help him find out whether he is still up to the job. Given recent events, he i</span>
  <span id="freeText2224511821542738235" style="display:none">‘Skin. The largest human organ, it is also the most overlooked.’<br />Dr David Hunter is still recovering from a near-fatal attack, and has left London temporarily to spend time at the Anthropology Research Facility in Knoxville, Tennessee.<br /> <br />‘Most people just called it the Body Farm’.<br /><br />This is where David Hunter first trained in forensic anthropology, and he hopes that this return trip will restore his shattered confidence and help him find out whether he is still up to the job. Given recent events, he is still bearing emotional and physical scars and he hasn’t worked for some months.<br /><br />When his former mentor, Tom Lieberman, invites him to assist on a murder investigation, he agrees: after all, he’ll only be an observer.<br /><br />But in this case, nothing is at it seems. The victim has been bound and tortured, and the body has decomposed beyond recognition - far more than it should have given the timeframe. There are fingerprints at the scene – but do they really identify the killer? Trying to track down the killer leads to the discovery of another body is found and it soon becomes clear that nothing is straightforward in this investigation. When David Hunter points out some inconsistencies, he discovers that not everyone investigating is happy about his involvement. He is, after all, British not American.<br /><br />In the meantime, the killer is fascinated by death and what happens at the point of death and is not likely to stop killing. But who is the killer? How many people have they killed, and over what period of time? And how (and who) will stop the killer? When events escalate, the investigators realise that they are searching for a serial killer with a detailed knowledge of forensic pathology.<br /><br />‘Life’s too short.’<br /><br />This is Simon Beckett’s third book (of four so far published) to feature forensic anthropologist David Hunter. I enjoyed this novel, as I have the other three, but did not much care for the italicised passages from the mind of the killer. For me, those passages slowed down the narrative without adding much value to the story.<br /><br />Jennifer Cameron-Smith<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2224511821542738235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2130215-kate?shelf=forensic-anthropology">forensic-anthropology</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2934824423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2418500406124105844">"A field of corpses laid out in a macabre display ... A serial killer who confounds even the most seasoned profilers ... A doctor whose life has been shattered by crime -- plunged into the heart of a shocking investigation ... forensic anthropologist David Hunter is thrust into his first murder investigation on U.S. soil -- and his most devastating case yet.<br/><br/>"In the heat of a Tennessee summer, Dr. Hunter has come to Knoxville's legendary 'Body Farm' -- the infamous field laboratory where law enfo</span>
  <span id="freeText2418500406124105844" style="display:none">"A field of corpses laid out in a macabre display ... A serial killer who confounds even the most seasoned profilers ... A doctor whose life has been shattered by crime -- plunged into the heart of a shocking investigation ... forensic anthropologist David Hunter is thrust into his first murder investigation on U.S. soil -- and his most devastating case yet.<br /><br />"In the heat of a Tennessee summer, Dr. Hunter has come to Knoxville's legendary 'Body Farm' -- the infamous field laboratory where law enforcement personnel study real corpses -- to escape London and the violence that nearly destroyed his life. He's also here to find out if he's still up to the job of sorting through death in all its strange and terrible forms ... Hunter will soon find his answer when he's called to a crime scene in a remote Smoky Mountains cabin -- a scene as grisly as it is bizarre.<br /><br />"The body is taped to a table. Everything about the crime scene -- the wounds, the decomposition, the microscopic evidence -- quickly short-circuits the tools and methods of forensic experts. Within days, Hunter knows he's dealing with a serial killer, someone intimately familiar with the intricacies of forensics. All around him, egos and hierarchies clash -- from the boasts of a renowned criminal profiler to the dogged work of a young female investigator -- but fate keeps pushing Hunter further into the heart of the manhunt. And the killer keeps coming up with surprises: booby-trapping corpses, faking times of death, swapping bodies -- finally turning his sights on Hunter himself ...<br /><br />"An electrifying race against time, a fascinating journey into the world of forensic science, a terrifying portrait of a killer in love with death itself, <i>Whispers of the Dead</i> is a thriller of the highest order."<br /><br />It certainly was hair-raising enough. And the closer to the end, the more surprises and the more death and danger. Crime horror (or whatever this genre is called) usually isn't my favorite, and this one was a difficult read for me. I like forensic anthropology, but not gruesome. And this one was. Let's hope the author gets back to "ordinary" forensic anthropology in the next book.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_989791319" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989791319" />
    <a title="Dan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7325648-dan"><img alt="Dan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586786063p2/7325648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/989791319?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan" href="/user/show/7325648-dan">Dan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7325648-dan?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer989791319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5895878411873551635">This is, finally, the novel I knew Simon Beckett was capable of writing. The first two David Hunter novels were full of potential but for various reasons they never quite lived up to it. This time though Beckett really nails it. <br/><br/>Forensic anthropologist David Hunter has returned to the infamous "body farm" in Tennessee for some research and an excuse to get away from the country. Suddenly he finds himself joining old friend Tom in a homicide investigation which very soon spirals out of control. T</span>
  <span id="freeText5895878411873551635" style="display:none">This is, finally, the novel I knew Simon Beckett was capable of writing. The first two David Hunter novels were full of potential but for various reasons they never quite lived up to it. This time though Beckett really nails it. <br /><br />Forensic anthropologist David Hunter has returned to the infamous "body farm" in Tennessee for some research and an excuse to get away from the country. Suddenly he finds himself joining old friend Tom in a homicide investigation which very soon spirals out of control. There's a dangerous killer on the loose and no-one is safe.<br /><br />The forensic anthropologist angle of the books has always been the best thing and once again Beckett makes gruesomely good use of it, having David investigate hugely decomposed corpses. The main character has often been a little bland but thanks to the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1328721.Written_in_Bone__David_Hunter__2_" title="Written in Bone (David Hunter #2) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Written in Bone</a> he is more interesting here, a man falling apart thanks to trauma and heartbreak. It's just levelled enough to make us sympathise with him without getting fed up of his anxiety. <br /><br />There are two big factors which can really make a good individual crime book and those are a clever mystery and a well characterised-murderer. The mystery here not the cleverest ever but some of the details are both disturbing and works of genius. It's the killer though that really makes this book, a serial killer who kills because death fascinates him. There are second-person sections from his point of view, which characterise him well but really ought to have been in the first-person. It's actually the psychological analysis from the homicide team that really give us his character and he is one of the most disturbing murderers I have ever read about. And he could feasibly be nearly any of the characters.<br /><br />An excellent and really dark thriller, certainly not one for the light-hearted. It is often said that the Americans do everything bigger and better than the Brits and Here David Hunter fins out that includes serial killers...</span>
  <a data-text-id="5895878411873551635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14237758723384385571">This book was pretty good, along the same lines as the first two in this series.   <span id="freeText14237758723384385571" style="display:none">This book was pretty good, along the same lines as the first two in this series. I believe that the narration from the point of view of the perpetrator was completely unnecessary and it would have been a better book without it. As this book is set in the US, the author should have consulted an American about the dialog he put in the mouths of the American characters. Americans don't use the word "result" as frequently or in the same way the British do. If they found out who fingerprints belonged to they would call it a match not a result. There are some other examples but this was the most glaring.</span>

<div id="review_339352240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/339352240" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339352240?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/3049657-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385340069" href="/book/show/6045290-whispers-of-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3049657-victoria?shelf=books-in-a-series">books-in-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3049657-victoria?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339352240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17590875255857607097">The third volume in the David Hunter series isn't quite as thrilling as the second book, unfortunately, The change of scenery was interesting, though - but maybe that was part of why I didn't enjoy it quite as much... I think that the dramatic ending of the second installment had me expecting a different sort of continuation, and this one just didn't pick up where I expected it to which let me down a bit. Still, I am interested in seeing what happens next in the series - it's a solid series and </span>
  <span id="freeText17590875255857607097" style="display:none">The third volume in the David Hunter series isn't quite as thrilling as the second book, unfortunately, The change of scenery was interesting, though - but maybe that was part of why I didn't enjoy it quite as much... I think that the dramatic ending of the second installment had me expecting a different sort of continuation, and this one just didn't pick up where I expected it to which let me down a bit. Still, I am interested in seeing what happens next in the series - it's a solid series and the ending twist has become something of a trademark over these last three books. </span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1503822686" />
    <a title="Bexy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11252121-bexy"><img alt="Bexy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343160314p2/11252121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1503822686?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bexy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bexy" href="/user/show/11252121-bexy">Bexy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1503822686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10362662162661981902">So this novel takes a different approach and have to say am not sure it fully works. This time its a more contemporary style thriller about a serial killer (which is what I like), however this story really feels long and drawn out, so by the time you get to the final twist - it's basically a bit of a let down. Overall it seems like this is a first attempt at this style of storytelling, certainly nothing like his first novel. Overall 3 stars, not bad for a raining afternoon but no real sparks for</span>
  <span id="freeText10362662162661981902" style="display:none">So this novel takes a different approach and have to say am not sure it fully works. This time its a more contemporary style thriller about a serial killer (which is what I like), however this story really feels long and drawn out, so by the time you get to the final twist - it's basically a bit of a let down. Overall it seems like this is a first attempt at this style of storytelling, certainly nothing like his first novel. Overall 3 stars, not bad for a raining afternoon but no real sparks for me.....</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_18487675'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18487675-noah"><img alt="Noah" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1379151410l/18487675._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NwZ2lqGJbwXvv5KIZIwQ6rG+qvITLMUKOecPPPRMhuV26QykYNC086TpbE951RELpTv/IWr69YbxKuFGsunJaw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XAjaIjJa0qoVlZmRxKEjow9iJyf/fhu8oRP/IJHAj2kd56AQ8wMJXF7DZ1bZ+CJCG+dy9IaoKzBp3hFa12XA5w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14945437988318568354">After an MA in English, Simon Beckett spent several years as a property repairer before a stint teaching in Spain. Back in the UK, he played percussion in several bands. He has been a freelance journalist since 1992, writing for The Times, The Independent on Sunday Review, The Daily Telegraph, The Observer and other major British publications. In 2002, as part of an article on the National Forensi</span>
  <span id="freeText14945437988318568354" style="display:none">After an MA in English, Simon Beckett spent several years as a property repairer before a stint teaching in Spain. Back in the UK, he played percussion in several bands. He has been a freelance journalist since 1992, writing for The Times, The Independent on Sunday Review, The Daily Telegraph, The Observer and other major British publications. In 2002, as part of an article on the National Forensic Academy, he visited the Body Farm in Tennessee. This last commission was the inspiration behind the internationally bestselling The Chemistry of Death, which was shortlisted for the CWA's Duncan Lawrie Dagger and has been translated into 21 languages. Simon Beckett is married and lives in Sheffield. The author of six novels, his second David Hunter thriller, Written in Bone, is published as a Bantam paperback in April 2008.</span>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;All narcissists are self-obsessed, but malignant narcissists are at the top of the scale. They have a pathological self-belief—a sense of grandiosity, even—which demands attention and admiration. They're convinced they're special in some way and want other people to acknowledge it as well. Crucially, they're also sadists who lack any conscience. They don't necessarily get fulfilment from inflicting pain, but they enjoy the sense of power it gives them. And they're indifferent to any suffering they might cause.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
